<div id="review_467388794" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/467388794" />
    <a title="Barbara Elsborg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2050186-barbara-elsborg"><img alt="Barbara Elsborg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498220836p2/2050186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/467388794?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara Elsborg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara Elsborg" href="/user/show/2050186-barbara-elsborg">Barbara Elsborg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer467388794" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5028110714247474420">I bought this book for a number of reasons - liked the cover (call me shallow), liked the blurb, liked the little round sticker thing telling me it was a sexy romance. Sadly, that was more or less all I liked about it. It was YA. WHY didn't it say that on the book? I wouldn't have bought it. I don't want to read a romance involving a 17 year old. I've seen comments that say this is something that will appeal to older readers but it didn't appeal to me.<br/>The plot had so many holes it was laughable </span>
  <span id="freeText5028110714247474420" style="display:none">I bought this book for a number of reasons - liked the cover (call me shallow), liked the blurb, liked the little round sticker thing telling me it was a sexy romance. Sadly, that was more or less all I liked about it. It was YA. WHY didn't it say that on the book? I wouldn't have bought it. I don't want to read a romance involving a 17 year old. I've seen comments that say this is something that will appeal to older readers but it didn't appeal to me.<br />The plot had so many holes it was laughable at times. <br />The spelling and grammar mistakes made me cringe. Where was the editing? The author is attending a top British university and the mistakes are bad ones. Draw and drawer muddled. Missing apostrophes etc<br />The dialogue tags are ones all professional writers are told to avoid. <br />The repeats of words like smirked - are annoying.<br />The characters are even more annoying. <br />Why would she want Kaspar? He's horrible.<br />Why would he want her? She's insufferable. <br />She had the voice of an arrogant teenager floucing all over the place. He didn't sound like a century old vampire.<br />I could go on and on, I won't.<br />I did think some of the descriptions were well done. The ball, the dancing, the way she was passed from vamp to vamp was well written and chilling. <br />I know the author was very young when she started this and I commend her for actually writing a novel but she has to be judged on adult terms when a big publisher puts her on the shelves. I'll be writing to complain to them that they mislead with not stating this book is YA - or at least telling the potential reader the heroine is 17 in the blurb.<br />So I don't feel I'm the target audience and in that respect the review will seem harsh. I wish I'd found it compelling but I didn't.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5028110714247474420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_412192342" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/412192342" />
    <a title="Vasya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4547586-vasya"><img alt="Vasya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324834504p2/4547586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/412192342?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vasya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vasya" href="/user/show/4547586-vasya">Vasya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062248749" href="/book/show/15983701-dinner-with-a-vampire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4547586-vasya?shelf=fantasy-paranormal">fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4547586-vasya?shelf=netgalley-arc">netgalley-arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer412192342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8403540478638103783">First, I would like to say that I've read this story on wattpad.com before it was published, so some of my references in this review might be a little bit confusing to some, but I will try to clear it up as much as I can.<br/><br/>Second, I've been a fan of Canse12 (aka the author) for a while and I never would have guessed that the story is inspired by Twilight. I mean, There is just no connection that my mind can grasp and establish between the two works other than it revolves around vampires, and that </span>
  <span id="freeText8403540478638103783" style="display:none">First, I would like to say that I've read this story on wattpad.com before it was published, so some of my references in this review might be a little bit confusing to some, but I will try to clear it up as much as I can.<br /><br />Second, I've been a fan of Canse12 (aka the author) for a while and I never would have guessed that the story is inspired by Twilight. I mean, There is just no connection that my mind can grasp and establish between the two works other than it revolves around vampires, and that is even a greater blasphemy of this work in connection to the Twilight, because this one actually has backbone. The world the Varns live in, the dimensions, the blood and gore is incomparable to Twilight, so if you are a fan of it, don't expect anything similar to this book. If you're not a fan, read it because you won't find anything similar in it.<br /><br />Now, the story is great. From it's rough draft to it's published version, it simply enchanted me and I never would have guessed, although I hoped, that it would come this far. I love Violet, I love Kaspar, and almost everything in this novel has a kaspary feel to it. <br /><br />I gave it four stars instead of five because there were some inconsistencies in the book that were rather obvious to me because I've read the draft, but that won't be to those who are not familiar with the work Gibbs published on wattpad. There are some references to events that have not occurred in this version or are slightly different <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she's not raped, although she mentions it later in the story and the relationship with Joel is not made known until she sees him, but then she speaks to Kaspar as if he knew it from the beginning - it was just weird <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> - and there were just enough of those mistakes that I just couldn't enjoy it to the fullest, as I would have liked. I also had a problem with the roundabout way everything near the end worked out - it was a tad too slow for it to be a culmination point worthy of an epic ending - but I liked it in the end and I do plan on reading the next book.<br /><br />I am quite happy that this book has got it's ending. I always felt that I left something unfinished with it, but now I am able to bring it to a type of closure, because I will be waiting for that sequel - and I sincerely hope that it will come soon.<br /><br />P.S.Kaspary: a level of awesomeness so high it kicks everyone’s arse leaving them breathless and bewildered - just so you know the definition :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8403540478638103783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_417964105" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/417964105" />
    <a title="All Things Urban Fantasy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy"><img alt="All Things Urban Fantasy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320345194p2/2732683.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/417964105?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="All Things Urban Fantasy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="All Things Urban Fantasy" href="/user/show/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy">All Things Urban Fantasy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer417964105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5181261517940306405">I should have known better. THE DARK HEROINE began as Twilight fan fiction in the mind of then fifteen year old Abigail Gibbs. Three years later, hot on the heels of another Twilight-fan-fiction-turned-huge-best-seller, Harper Voyager is publishing this sloppy, poorly written, and often upsetting mess.<br/>Violet witnesses a vampire attack, and the vampires decide to abduct the witness and keep her at their family estate until she dies or agrees to turn. The Cullens they are not. They intimidate, thr</span>
  <span id="freeText5181261517940306405" style="display:none">I should have known better. THE DARK HEROINE began as Twilight fan fiction in the mind of then fifteen year old Abigail Gibbs. Three years later, hot on the heels of another Twilight-fan-fiction-turned-huge-best-seller, Harper Voyager is publishing this sloppy, poorly written, and often upsetting mess.<br />Violet witnesses a vampire attack, and the vampires decide to abduct the witness and keep her at their family estate until she dies or agrees to turn. The Cullens they are not. They intimidate, threaten, and assault Violet regularly. Kasper is basically a sexual predator with fangs. He tells Violet that he will have sex with her eventually whether she wants to or not. He has has loud, wall shaking sex every night in the room next to her. At one point he even breaks down her door and attacks her when she thwarts his “date” plans one night, pins her to the bed–in front of his ‘date’–and threatens to ‘use her instead’:<br /><br /><blockquote>In a blur he launched himself across the room. He collided with my side to take me with him, and I was sent rolling across the bed, coming to a halt when my head hit the bedside cabinet. I let out a scream as he landed on top of me, pinning me to the bed. I winced through gritted teeth as the corner of the cabinet dug into my spine.<br />“Get off me, you horny git!” I screeched, kicking and flailing, revolted at his closeness.<br />“Why, am I making you uncomfortable? Maybe I will use you instead!” he snarled, a tormenting smirk twisting his face. His eyes were devoid of any emotion—he meant it. Straddling me with one leg either side of my stomach, he forced me deeper into the mattress, pinning my hands above my head. He began to pull my shirt up, and I heard squeals of protest from Charity, which merged with the protests of the mattress as I tried to fight free.</blockquote><br /><br />The breaking point for me comes when Violet is brutally attacked, and sexually assaulted by another vicious and psychotic vampire. He says and does truly abhorrent things to her including detailing his plan for necrophilia. A scant second before he rapes her, she is rescued by Kasper. Days later, they have their first sexual encounter when Kasper attacks her in her sleep:<br /><br /><blockquote>He snarled, hastily clamping a hand down over my mouth. I attempted to bite at his fingers but found myself quickly subdued.<br />“Play nicely now,” he mocked, pressing himself closer. I caught sight of the deranged, lustful glint in his blood-red eyes. My eyes widened and I was hushed to silence, terrified.<br />“Come on, Girly, just a little drop of blood. I’m so hungry. You’ll enjoy it.”<br />I scowled and thrashed about as he lay draped across me, pressing his crotch hard into my stomach.</blockquote><br /><br />It just got worse from there and I gave up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5181261517940306405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_440341789" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/440341789" />
    <a title="Emily (Falling for YA)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4788621-emily-falling-for-ya"><img alt="Emily (Falling for YA)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551209496p2/4788621.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/440341789?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily (Falling for YA)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily (Falling for YA)" href="/user/show/4788621-emily-falling-for-ya">Emily (Falling for YA)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4788621-emily-falling-for-ya?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4788621-emily-falling-for-ya?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer440341789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18344250564066751495">*This is a review for an New Adult/Adult book<br/><br/>I requested this title on Edelweiss because I was curious. I had heard this was originally written on Wattpad when the author was 15 and was later picked up by a major publishing house in a six figure deal. That is enough to stir anyone's curiosity. Unfortunately, curiosity can also get you in trouble and that was the case for me.<br/><br/>First off this isn’t going to be a nice review. I had so many problems with this book that is was impossible for me to enjo</span>
  <span id="freeText18344250564066751495" style="display:none">*This is a review for an New Adult/Adult book<br /><br />I requested this title on Edelweiss because I was curious. I had heard this was originally written on Wattpad when the author was 15 and was later picked up by a major publishing house in a six figure deal. That is enough to stir anyone's curiosity. Unfortunately, curiosity can also get you in trouble and that was the case for me.<br /><br />First off this isn’t going to be a nice review. I had so many problems with this book that is was impossible for me to enjoy. To illustrate my point I am going to do something a little different for this review, I am going to review it using my Goodreads status updates so that you can see exactly what I was feeling as I progressed through this novel.<br /><br />1. Page 1 "There are so many mixed reviews about this book I'm both nervous and excited to read it. I will keep my expectations low so I can either be pleasantly surprised or not disappointed."<br /><br />See look! I started this book off with some apprehension but was going to keep my expectations low so that I didn’t get hurt.<br /><br />2. P 61 "Is this book YA or NA? Its ok so far, a little wordy but I'm intrigued."<br /><br />I found out as I continued reading that I would probably class this book as New Adult because the protagonist is 18 and there is sexual content. Also the wordiness NEVER STOPS. It was like the publisher just took exactly what was on Wattpad and never edited it. The purpose of editing is to take out the parts that aren’t needed or do not advance the story, unfortunately that never happens in this book and instead we are left with a wordy, disjointed and lengthy novel.<br /><br />3. P.331 "Well this is taking a turn for the weird/disturbing. I actually think I hate all of the charterers in this book. No one has a redeeming quality. And now the girl with Stockholm syndrome is sleeping with the kidnapper who is a complete jackass, great."<br /><br />This is the heart of why I hated this book. None of the characters were likable. None of them had a redeeming quality. The heroine, Violet Lee, witnesses a vampire murder and then to keep her silent the vampires take her back to their mansion. While at the mansion she falls for Kaspar (Stockholm Syndrome much?). Kaspar treats women, vampire and human alike terribly and then for some reason these two absolutely terribly people fall for eachother. I think at one point there is also an edict from Kaspar’s father that they can’t touch. I mean things just got SO ridiculous and disjointed the story became painful to read. <br /><br />I also want to mention that this book has the honor of having the least sexy sex scene that I have ever read. There was no passion, no emotion it was completely blasé and sort of grossed me out to be honest. With this scene you could really tell that someone young and inexperienced was writing it. <br /><br />4. P.381 "I'm debating whether to stop reading this but I feel like I've already made it this far...also random aside this whole Dark Heroine business feels like a completely different story that was just tacked on to the one I began. No foreshadowing or linking things up so they flow."<br /><br />Randomly during the last quarter of the book Gibbs stops focusing on the relationship/problems between Kaspar, Violet, and Kaspar’s family and begins focusing on a Dark Heroine prophesy. It came completely out of left field and didn’t link up to the story at all! If the story had focused on the Dark Heroine from the beginning it actually might have been an interesting story. <br /><br />Overall, I did eventually finish the story but it took months and it was the worst book I have read in recent memory. The story had good potential but was poorly executed and even more poorly edited. I think Gibbs has potential as an author with a little polish and a serious editor. Hopefully her next novel someone takes all this potential and turns it in to something worthwhile.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18344250564066751495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_421991350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/421991350" />
    <a title="Mara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3954707-mara"><img alt="Mara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329760375p2/3954707.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421991350?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mara" href="/user/show/3954707-mara">Mara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062248749" href="/book/show/15983701-dinner-with-a-vampire">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421991350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11278582723493087472">Update: I rated it. Can't say it's a book I liked nor I connected to it in any way (so no 2 stars): <strong>1 1/2</strong><br/><br/>Hush, hush. I know, GR. You did warn me. This is fan-fic being published after the Book That Shall Not Be Named became famous. This is sparkly going dark and vegetarianism being swapped.<br/><br/>Reading this book was like watching a train wreck or the scene of a big road incident. You stare in horrified fascination. You are ashamed of yourself for it. You know you should turn away and respect the dead</span>
  <span id="freeText11278582723493087472" style="display:none">Update: I rated it. Can't say it's a book I liked nor I connected to it in any way (so no 2 stars): <strong>1 1/2</strong><br /><br />Hush, hush. I know, GR. You did warn me. This is fan-fic being published after the Book That Shall Not Be Named became famous. This is sparkly going dark and vegetarianism being swapped.<br /><br />Reading this book was like watching a train wreck or the scene of a big road incident. You stare in horrified fascination. You are ashamed of yourself for it. You know you should turn away and respect the dead, but no way you can.<br /><br />At the moment I can't give it a rating. Because I found it terribly bad, but I did read it all and I couldn't stop. As I said "horrified but fascinated". This is YA, definitely YA, but with sex in it....I can't even tag it. It's not YA: violence, rape and sex are not exactly right for it. It's not urban fantasy: where's my kickass H/h?. I can't even say it's PNR as I doubt this is love. <br /><br />If this story had been a poem, it would have no sense or rhyme. The plot is full of holes, the characters are terribly deja-vu (ie Amanda Hockins, just to name the less famous...), juvenile is almost a compliment if I have to think about the voice. <br /><br />Spoilery<br /><br />Holes in plot and world-building: <br />-There is no need for her "prison term" once she is known as the daughter of a government official. (The powers that be know of the existence of vamps.) So the same beginning of the book is based on shaking foundations.<br />-They get punished because they have sex. Above all she is, because she knew she shouldn't have gotten involved with the family. ...Err. How? When was this said, explained, inferred? <br />-She understands of all a sudden what her father did (when nobody else could). Again how? Because of dates? You believe your father is a murderer on something this flimsy and without explanations? There is no explanation of how she gets to this conclusion. We are told she did and buried this knowledge. And that's it.<br />-Death penalty scene. How could anyone know about her secret?<br /><br /><br />Characters: the only thing you can say about her is feisty. There's nothing else: no brain, no real defiance. Sometime she read bipolar. I guess in her own way she is strong. But hell if there was a reason for her behaviour and depth to her. (And please: no more marysuism. Do we need every single heroine to be this special?) Him: snarly and jerky. Same as above. <br /><br />Relationship: abusive is being nice. Sociopath is a better tag. Find nearest stake, please.<br /><br />Writing voice: no nuances among characters. They all sound teenagers even when they are supposed to be a thousand year old.<br /><br />Worse of all? Yes this is fan-fic, but it has been published by Harper Collins. And I expect the level of control, being much, much better of a self-pub. I do not want to find missing words or to read things like "pressed pressing".<br /><br />A good thing?...<br />-the price. At 2.99 it makes the sting <em>slightly</em> less burning...<br />-the violence, in a sense. Vampires are dark beings, literally. No glitter on them, no romanticized versions. They are killers. They aren't made into something different. <br /><br /><br />Do you think she'll save the world? I'm not going to read the sequel, but I'm ready to bet on it. <br /><br />Sorry, I'm going. The roadkill made me sick. I need a scotch, a tumbler of whiskey, some rum. Hell, even a beer. Nope, a cuppa will be better. I really need to meditate on my choices... &lt; grin &gt;<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11278582723493087472" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_629624574" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/629624574" />
    <a title="Ashneet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15506821-ashneet"><img alt="Ashneet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442840176p2/15506821.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/629624574?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashneet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashneet" href="/user/show/15506821-ashneet">Ashneet</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer629624574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3455589039619894233">I absolutely adored this novel. I thought that the two protagonists were great. This novel is written in the POV of Violet Lee, which is our female protagonist and Kasper Varn who is our male protagonist. However there are considerably more chapters from Violets POV.<br/><br/>Violet is a headstrong, kick ass and all in all an awesome character. But their were moments where I was screaming at her. Kasper Varn however is just SEXY! that's all I have to say on him. He is just amazing!<br/><br/>I won't go into the plot</span>
  <span id="freeText3455589039619894233" style="display:none">I absolutely adored this novel. I thought that the two protagonists were great. This novel is written in the POV of Violet Lee, which is our female protagonist and Kasper Varn who is our male protagonist. However there are considerably more chapters from Violets POV.<br /><br />Violet is a headstrong, kick ass and all in all an awesome character. But their were moments where I was screaming at her. Kasper Varn however is just SEXY! that's all I have to say on him. He is just amazing!<br /><br />I won't go into the plot as you guys can just read the description but I can say that I was not satisfied with the end. The ending left me with a lot of questions that I wanted the answers to. However now that I know that their will be a sequel titled 'Autumn Rose', I hope those questions are finally answered. <br /><br />Overall I recommend you read this book as its entertaining and can be pretty funny at times. Also it's set in England which I thought was a good change as most YA novels are set in America. Even though this novel is about vampires and there are a million other vampire novels out already, I found this to be quite a unique take on them. All in all I think if you enjoy reading about vampires then I think you will like this novel. Also don't be intimidated by the size. I finished this novel in two days. It's an easy read so you will just fly right through it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3455589039619894233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_411566004" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/411566004" />
    <a title="Kara-karina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5427067-kara-karina"><img alt="Kara-karina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305236745p2/5427067.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/411566004?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kara-karina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kara-karina" href="/user/show/5427067-kara-karina">Kara-karina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer411566004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3867617999523696991"><br/>I'm obsessed with this book, peeps. I'm bullying my fellow bloggers to read it and I keep talking about it.<br/><br/>Thing is there are plenty of faults with the plot and writing in general, but it's just such a compelling, powerful and magical read, that I haven't noticed much of that while I was blazing through The Dark Heroine *grinning*<br/><br/>First of all, it's a gritty, violent, sexy and pretty raw read. The main character, 17 year-old Violet is not a damsel in distress, she is a daughter of a powerful man </span>
  <span id="freeText3867617999523696991" style="display:none"><br />I'm obsessed with this book, peeps. I'm bullying my fellow bloggers to read it and I keep talking about it.<br /><br />Thing is there are plenty of faults with the plot and writing in general, but it's just such a compelling, powerful and magical read, that I haven't noticed much of that while I was blazing through The Dark Heroine *grinning*<br /><br />First of all, it's a gritty, violent, sexy and pretty raw read. The main character, 17 year-old Violet is not a damsel in distress, she is a daughter of a powerful man who just happened to be in a wrong place in the wrong time. She sees a massacre of vampire hunters by a bunch of young arrogant vampires, who sweep her away to their manor in the countryside. The rule is: humans who know of their existence are killed or turned. However, when vamps find out who Violet's father is, either choice will bring both societies on a brink of war.<br /><br />So, snarky, stubborn and get even Violet stays in the manor as a hostage, gets embroiled in complicated vampire politics and develops hate/love/weird friendship relationships with a young, vicious vampire prince, Kaspar Varn.<br /><br /> <blockquote> I did not move, still rubbing my chest. “My name is not ‘Girly’! It’s Violet!” <br /> Like a shot he was just inches away from me, forcing me against the wall as his hand wrapped around my neck. A single finger was pressed against my vein, stroking it.<br /> “And I’m the fucking Prince!” he snarled, grip tightening. My eyes widened and I struggled under him but his grip just tightened. I closed my eyes, not wanting to see his face, so close to mine and reeking of blood. A single image flooded my mind behind myclosed eyes: the lifeless body of Claude Pierre, crumpled and bleeding on the stone flag.<br /> “I could snap that pretty neck of yours in two with less effort than it would take for you to squeal,” he whispered in my ear. “So I suggest that you do what we say, because you can’t outrun us and the police won’t stop us.”</blockquote><br /><br /><br />Kaspar *sigh*, he is a a dreamy, dreamy monster. He is a proper anti-hero, and by all means I should have hated him for being a jerk and all. He kills, he maims, he is being cruel and cold, and yet at the same time, there are certain reasons for his behaviour, and the more he connects with Violet the more they are both changing. She acquires some of his ruthlessness and he softens up.<br /><br />According to urban dictionary, kaspary is a level of awesomeness so high it kicks you in the ass and leaves you breathless and bewildered. So here you go, Abigail Gibbs created a new word for us to use :D<br /><br />There is a complicated plot of vampire mannerisms and rituals, an ancient prophecy and even different dimensions, so I wouldn't call this book your average vampire YA. Oh, and the vampire balls are alien and magical!<br /><br />There is also plenty of violence and some sex involved, the latter shows how blatantly screwed modern teenager's views on women and how a girl should perceive herself. I don't blame Abigail for that because she writes what she knows, however it is sad that young girls feel that they deserve so little respect.<br /><br />The world Abigail Gibbs built is an ambitious one. It's also very flexible, so I wouldn't really know what to expect from the book two. It just reads like a twisted, dark fairy-tale. I only know that book #2 is on my autobuy list and that this 18 year old British author has a wonderful potential for growth, if she can write like that at her age.<br /><br />Very much recommended. I...uhm... even made a playlist for this book on YouTube. Embarrassing, I know...</span>
  <a data-text-id="3867617999523696991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  </div>

<div id="review_421101697" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/421101697" />
    <a title="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life"><img alt="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563622982p2/3024878.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421101697?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" href="/user/show/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life">Donna {Book Passion For Life}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life?shelf=adult-newadult-paranormal">adult-newadult-paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421101697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15758283754540324847"><b>He sighed, his hands tangling themselves in my already-knotted hair. “Violet, don’t ever leave me. Whatever happens; however things get, just don’t go. Please.”</b><br/><br/><b>4.5 stars</b> <br/><br/><i>The Dark Heroine</i> is an absolutely fantastic debut novel by author Abigail Gibbs. I had no idea that this author was only 15-years-old when she wrote this novel, and wow, does she have a talent because this is one exciting page turner. <br/><br/>Violet Lee is a seventeen-year-old who is trying to get over her failed relationship with her e</span>
  <span id="freeText15758283754540324847" style="display:none"><b>He sighed, his hands tangling themselves in my already-knotted hair. “Violet, don’t ever leave me. Whatever happens; however things get, just don’t go. Please.”</b><br /><br /><b>4.5 stars</b> <br /><br /><i>The Dark Heroine</i> is an absolutely fantastic debut novel by author Abigail Gibbs. I had no idea that this author was only 15-years-old when she wrote this novel, and wow, does she have a talent because this is one exciting page turner. <br /><br />Violet Lee is a seventeen-year-old who is trying to get over her failed relationship with her ex-boyfriend. While out clubbing one night, Violet witness’s a horrific murder but it’s no ordinary murder, the people killed were murdered by – vampires. Violet’s world is turned upside from this discovery because a vampire called Kaspar, takes Violet as his prisoner and brings her home to his family. While there Violet finds herself trying to fight her attraction to Kaspar Varn – even though she despises everything he is. Not only that, but she starts suffering from weird dreams – one’s she knows are real. But how can dreams be real? Soon she finds out her life is being played out by fate and Kaspar is just as much as a part of it as her. <br /><br />I loved this book, absolutely loved it and author Abigail Gibbs really managed to suck me all the way through. At night time, I had to force myself to go to bed because otherwise I would have stayed up all night reading and that is not good – especially when I have to work the next day. <br /><br />I fell in love with everything about this novel, the characters, the setting, the romance, the danger – everything. <i>The Dark Heroine</i> really does have a little bit of everything for everyone. It’s full of suspense with exciting twists and turns, it’s full of intense and engaging scenes and the story really does manage to capture your heart and make you fall in love with it. <br /><br />Violet really is a great protagonist. She’s fun and feisty and even when she’s in trouble or even when she's sad, she tries to stand up for herself. She even puts herself in Kasper’s firing line by pulling a few pranks on him, now this may not seem bad, but if you’ve read this book then you will know that Kasper is not one to mess around with. He’s scary! I loved how she was willing to stand up to him because it made the story so much fun. Even though Kasper is scary and of course bad, there is a good side to him and that good side is really, really good. I loved sweet, loving, caring Kasper. I loved how he was with Violet even though there were so many problems in their way. I’m dying to see what comes next for them because they have some tough times ahead. <br /><br />I really struggled between rating this book a 4.5 rating and a 5, but I finally settled on 4.5 because even though I loved it, I still felt there was more room at the end of the story, that the author could have took. I guess I just wanted more of Violet and Kasper’s story because where it ended was a very important scene - I felt like there should of been a little bit more. Now I’m not sure how much more details we’ll get about Violet and Kasper because the next book; <i>Autumn Rose</i> is about another character but I’m praying we will see something from Violet and Kasper. <br /><br />Overall, <i>The Dark Heroine</i> is a dark and dangerous tale – one that is highly enjoyable and loveable and I will be keeping an eye out for more work by this author. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15758283754540324847" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_639735189" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/639735189" />
    <a title="Didi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6082482-didi"><img alt="Didi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459297426p2/6082482.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/639735189?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Didi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Didi" href="/user/show/6082482-didi">Didi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Didi by: </span>
      Shreya
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=enemies-to-lovers">enemies-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=betrayal">betrayal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=my-captor-lover">my-captor-lover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=my-vampire-lover">my-vampire-lover</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer639735189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10514179863284524655">What to say, what to say...<br/><br/>I liked this book. For quite a few reasons. But I didn't love it like I hoped I would and that has to do with two reasons.<br/><br/>First I'll get into why it was good. Vampires. Need I say more?! I love em' and will read almost anything with them. So that right there is the first reason I liked this book. I also appreciated the multi-layered plot and detailed world building. This was far from a one-dimensional story and you could get seriously lost in the intricacies of it all.</span>
  <span id="freeText10514179863284524655" style="display:none">What to say, what to say...<br /><br />I liked this book. For quite a few reasons. But I didn't love it like I hoped I would and that has to do with two reasons.<br /><br />First I'll get into why it was good. Vampires. Need I say more?! I love em' and will read almost anything with them. So that right there is the first reason I liked this book. I also appreciated the multi-layered plot and detailed world building. This was far from a one-dimensional story and you could get seriously lost in the intricacies of it all. In a good way!<br /><br />I liked our main characters, Violet and Kasper. They were not your traditional love at first sight type stuff, and despite their very volatile and shaky relationship in the beginning, they developed a slow building and strong love that was tested over and over again.<br /><br />There was however an underlining SOMETHING. It wasn't love or lust necessarily but something that paved the way for their eventual blossoming. And despite Violet questioning her fall into Stockholm Syndrome, it was way more than just a story about a girl falling for her captor.<br /><br />Even the secondary characters, which were many, were entertaining. But some were despicable. Fabian being the prime example. He was Violets' rock when things were confusing and scary in the beginning, her anchor in a new and disturbing world. But the minute something didn't go as he liked he turned on her. Viciously. Nice friend.<br /><br />Now for the things I didn't necessarily like. It felt too young. It started YA--I knew this before starting--but turned NA almost because Violet turned eighteen early on. Also there were some intimate scenes and sexually explicit descriptions that garnered the NA tag, so I was happy about that! But still, it felt too young for me.<br /><br />Maybe that had to do with the fact that acquiring vampire maturity happened at a certain age which was explained from the world buidling perspective. Therefore a lot of vamps were essentially young, not in vamp years but in appearance. <br /><br />The other thing that I didn't like a whole lot was Kasper's underused POV. The story was told primarily from Violet's POV with some chapters dedicated to Kasper's. But it wasn't enough. I wish is was more equal.<br /><br />Regarldess, Violet was a strong, fearless and passionate young woman. She often stood up for herself and took no bullshit from anyone. Kasper although quite the asshole in the beginning, slowly shed his jerk persona for a more refined and intelligent cool demeanor. He remained sweet to Violet through this however and I felt she was the ONE to trigger his heart to beat again, metaphorically speaking. Hope that doesn't sound too cheesy, but there it is.<br /><br />This actually reminded me of Kristen Ashley's The Three series. Not necessarily the events and characters but the overall quest for uniting vampires and humanity.<br /><br />Good book with a creative premise! <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10514179863284524655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_429926086" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/429926086" />
    <a title="Natalie Frampton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4640485-natalie-frampton"><img alt="Natalie Frampton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456786789p2/4640485.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/429926086?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Frampton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Frampton" href="/user/show/4640485-natalie-frampton">Natalie Frampton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer429926086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5971006996695616823"><br/>I was asked to review this book by the lovely people at Harper Voyager and boy I am so glad I said yes.<br/>This book grabbed me from page one and kept me right until the end.<br/>Whilst on a night out Violet is witness to a horrific slaughter of a group of men. As the witness Violet is kidnapped by the murderers and taken to a lavish estate. On arrival Violet learns these men are not ordinary they are vampires. *squeal* <br/>It turns out this isn't as simple as it first seems. Violet is the daughter of a powe</span>
  <span id="freeText5971006996695616823" style="display:none"><br />I was asked to review this book by the lovely people at Harper Voyager and boy I am so glad I said yes.<br />This book grabbed me from page one and kept me right until the end.<br />Whilst on a night out Violet is witness to a horrific slaughter of a group of men. As the witness Violet is kidnapped by the murderers and taken to a lavish estate. On arrival Violet learns these men are not ordinary they are vampires. *squeal* <br />It turns out this isn't as simple as it first seems. Violet is the daughter of a powerful man and there are more complications than anyone had hoped as everyone is thrown in to a whirlwind of vampire-human politics. <br /><br />Violet is a beautiful character, she has spunk and courage where others would have given up. She portrays herself as tough but she is troubled and vulnerable. She hates the situation she has been thrown into and hates the vampires even more. As time progresses she finds herself making friends with several vampires but still loathes Kasper who was the one who decided to kidnap her rather than kill her.<br />Kasper is harsh and often cruel to Violet but he soon realises that isn't working. He is ultimately trying to get her to turn into a vampire and forcing her isn't going to work. <br />No matter how hard either of them try they are drawn to each other. Kasper is exciting and dangerous but he has a really sweet side. The side that every girl wants in a guy. He is protective and attentive to her needs and Violet soon finds herself falling for him.<br /><br />It's hard to find the words to express how much I loved this book. <br />I was really swept away by the story, I loved the Varnley estate and I felt I was experiencing everything as if I was right there with them. <br />I laughed, I cried and didn't want it to end. <br />Do yourself a favour and buy this book.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5971006996695616823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_440330874" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/440330874" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7297150-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325438214p2/7297150.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/440330874?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/7297150-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7297150-amy?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer440330874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2052925170279031623">I really wanted to like this book but it really disappointed me on so many levels. Whilst I can see that this could have been an interesting premise and a unique take on vampires- it wasn't. Unfortunately this book was badly plotted, written without maturity (I know that the author is young, but in my opinion this was not of a high enough quality to publish. What were HarperCollins thinking?!), and sadly the story boiled down to bad Twilight fanfiction. As for other reviews that maintain that th</span>
  <span id="freeText2052925170279031623" style="display:none">I really wanted to like this book but it really disappointed me on so many levels. Whilst I can see that this could have been an interesting premise and a unique take on vampires- it wasn't. Unfortunately this book was badly plotted, written without maturity (I know that the author is young, but in my opinion this was not of a high enough quality to publish. What were HarperCollins thinking?!), and sadly the story boiled down to bad Twilight fanfiction. As for other reviews that maintain that there are no similarities between this story and Twilight- may I draw your attention to the main female character, a pale skinned, dark haired girl who seems to hold an allure to every male character that she meets in the book. And if that wasn't enough- how about the lead male character, a vampire with an old-fashioned name, over 100 years old, who enjoys dancing and often hunts animals (at one point in the book we see him hunt a rabbit). Oh- and did I mention, his eyes change colour!!! Seriously?! <br />Clearly the author has tried to change the story enough to make it her own but it just doesn't work. <br />So fellow GoodReaders- don't waste your pennies on this book! And if you really want to read it, for curiosity's sake?... You can have my copy, because I don't want it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2052925170279031623" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jOkdwg9U2Yqf6R5fUD9zt3EuCTsuzchU3jd4e2hcfOReIZSo7/PopQE8ilnc8Gpa3BYmX4GRw/ZFegJp+SijLw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iNoZPAylDWxmCtGc49aFd/O7vFFZfETtGlkWlVyDapBaEpBW7AI8Q/jfRZpvGZyaXoOTNfYgT0+BFGyHzfe1Ww==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer7929016376147476737">Abigail Gibbs was born and raised in deepest, darkest Devon. She is currently studying for a BA in English at the University of Oxford and considers herself a professional student, as the real world is yet to catch up with her. Her greatest fear is blood and she is a great advocate of vegetarianism, which logically led to the writing of her first novel, Dinner With A Vampire. At age fifteen, she b</span>
  <span id="freeText7929016376147476737" style="display:none">Abigail Gibbs was born and raised in deepest, darkest Devon. She is currently studying for a BA in English at the University of Oxford and considers herself a professional student, as the real world is yet to catch up with her. Her greatest fear is blood and she is a great advocate of vegetarianism, which logically led to the writing of her first novel, Dinner With A Vampire. At age fifteen, she began posting serially online under the pseudonym Canse12, and after three years in the internet limelight, set her sights towards total world domination. She splits her time between her studies, stories and family, and uses coffee to survive all three. </span>
